Proof from Supplication and Derivation of Power and Will
Maturidi uses supplication to prove choice, then derives power and will from choice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how universal supplication to God points to His choice, and how choice necessarily implies power and will.

Core Idea
People naturally pray to God for help, showing they believe He acts by choice, not compulsion.

Maturidi next turns to a universal human practice: supplication and earnest prayer. People from all cultures seek God's help for specific outcomes, which presupposes that God can freely choose to grant or withhold. He then argues that if God acts by choice, He must possess power (qudra) to act and will (irada) to determine specific acts. This lesson covers the supplication argument and the inference to divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the supplication argument
Read the Arabic and translation describing how people pray to God for relief, victory, and help.
Focus on the phrase 'دل ذلك على أن العالم باختياره'.
2
Understand the inference from choice to power and will
Maturidi says: when choice is established, power and will are established. Ask yourself: why does choice require both ability and specific intention?
Without power, action is disordered; without will, it is random.
3
Relate to the shahid/gha'ib principle
Maturidi uses the witnessed world (shahid) as a basis for understanding the unseen (gha'ib). True action in the witnessed world requires choice, power, and will.
This is a key method in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن الله تعالى إذ أنشأ شيء ثم أفناه ، وفيه أيضا ما قد أعاده نحو الليل والنهار ، ثبت أن فعله بالإختيار ؛ إذ تحقق به صلاح ما قد أفسده ، وإعادة ما قد أفناه ، وإيجاد المعدوم واعدام الموجود ، فثبت أن طريق ذلك الإختيار ؛ إذ من كان الذى منه يكون بالطبع لا يجيء منه نفي ما يوجد ، وإيجاد ما يعلمه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأيضا إنا قد بينا حدث العالم لا من شيء ، وذلك نوع ما لا يبلغه إلا فعل من هو في غاية معنى الإختيار ، وما يكون بالطبع فحقه الإضطرار ، ومحال أن يكون من يبلغ شأنه إلى إنشاء الأشياء لا من شيء ، ثم يكون ذلك بالطبع ما كان وقوع الشيء بالطبع هو تحت قهر آخر ، وجعله بحيث يسقط عنه الإمكان ، وذلك آية الحدث وأمارة الضعف ، جل ربنا عن ذلك وتعالى . ما جرى التعارف المتوارث من الخلق بالدعوات والتضرع إلى الله تعالى بالفرج مع وأنه قهر كذا ونصر كذا ، وأعان فلانا وخذل فلانا ، وأن كل ذي قوة يفعل بقوة أنشأها ، ولا ينال شيء من ذلك بالمضطر ، ولا يرغب فيه ؛ دل ذلك على أن العالم باختياره . فإذا ثبت الإختيار ثبتت له القدرة على الخلق ، والإرادة لكونه على ما هو عليه ؛ لأن من لا قدرة له يخرج الذى يكون منه مضطربا فاسدا ، ولا يملك الشيء وضده، فثبت أن ما كان منه بقدرة كان واختيار ، وذلك أمارات الفعل الحقيقية في الشاهد الذى هو أصل للعلم بالغائب ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى ما ذكرنا من تواصل الفعل - أعنى الواقع به بالفعل - وتتابعه محكما هو الدليل أنه كان فعله على العلم به، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأيضا أنه إذ خرج كل الجواهر التي لا يمتحن في مصالح الممتحنين ، وخلق كل شيء أريد به البقاء ، مع خلق ما به بقاؤه ، علم أنه كان بمن كيفية كل شيء وحاجته وما به القوام والمعاش ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأيضا أن الله سبحانه خلق الخلق خلقا دل على حدثه ، وعلى أن له محدثا ، وعلى وحدانية محدثه ، فلولا أن علم بالخلق - يعلم أنه إذا خلق على ما خلق كان فيه دليل العلم به وبخلقه - لا يحتمل أن يخرج على ذلك خلقه ، وبالله التوفيق
And also that God (exalted is He) when He created a thing then annihilated it, and also in it He has restored it like night and day, it is established that His action is by choice, because by it He achieves the rectification of what He corrupted, the restoration of what He annihilated, the bringing into existence of the non-existent and the annihilating of the existent. So it is established that the way of that is choice, for he from whom [action] occurs by nature cannot bring about the negation of what exists and the existence of what he knows, and there is no power except with God. And also we have already explained the origination (huduth) of the world from nothing, and that is a kind that no one can achieve except an act of one who is in the extreme sense of choice. And that which is by nature, its right is necessity, and it is impossible that the state of the one whose affair reaches the creation of things from nothing, then that is by nature, since the occurrence of a thing by nature is under the compulsion of another, making it such that possibility falls away from it; that is a sign of origination and a mark of weakness. Our Lord is exalted above that. What has occurred of inherited customary practice among creation of supplications and earnest prayers to God (exalted is He) for relief, and that He overpowers such and such, helps such and such, and aids so-and-so and forsakes so-and-so, and that every possessor of power acts with a power that He created, and nothing of that is attained by the compelled one, nor is it desired—that indicates that the world is by His choice. So when choice is established, then power over creation is established for Him, and will (irada) for His being as He is. Because whoever has no power, his action comes out disturbed and corrupt, and he does not possess a thing and its opposite. So it is established that what comes from Him by power is by choice, and that is the indicator of true action in the witnessed world (shahid) which is the basis for knowledge of the unseen (gha'ib). And there is no power except with God. And according to what we mentioned of the continuity of action—I mean occurring by it actually—and its sequence being perfect, it is the evidence that His action was with knowledge of it. And there is no power except with God. And also that since every substance that is not tested in the interests of those tested, and He created everything intended for permanence, along with creating what is necessary for its permanence, it is known that He knows the 'how' of everything and its need and what sustains it and livelihood. And there is no power except with God. And also that God (exalted is He) created creatures in a way that indicates their origination, and that they have a creator, and the oneness of their creator. So if He had no knowledge of creation—knowing that when He creates in a certain way, there is in it evidence of knowledge of Him and His creation—it would not be possible for His creation to come out in that way. And success is from God.
Source pages p. 643

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rational proofs that God's actions are by choice (ikhtiyar), then derives the attributes of power (qudra), will (irada), and knowledge ('ilm). The author begins with the observation that God creates things and then annihilates them, then restores them (like the cycle of night and day). This ability to alternate states shows choice, because natural processes cannot reverse themselves in such a purposeful manner. Next, he appeals to creation ex nihilo (huduth al-‘alam la min shay'), which is an act only possible for a being with utmost choice; nature acts by necessity and compulsion. He then points to the universal practice of supplication (du'a) and prayer to God for specific outcomes—people naturally seek help from God, not from a compelled force, indicating that God acts by choice. From choice, he infers power and will: choice implies the ability to perform or not perform an act (qudra) and the specific determination of that act (irada). He argues that without power, action would be disordered, and that true power enables a thing and its opposite. Then he uses the consistent and flawless order in creation to prove that God acts with knowledge ('ilm). The argument is based on the principle that an orderly, purposeful sequence cannot arise from ignorance; it must be known. Finally, he notes that the very fact that creation points to its own createdness and to the oneness of its Creator presupposes knowledge on the part of the Creator. This lesson demonstrates the classical kalam method of proving divine attributes through rational inference from observable phenomena.

Key Terms
الدعوات
القدرة
الإرادة
الشاهد
الغائب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's actions might be random or without purpose.
Correction: Choice implies specific intention (will), so God's acts are purposeful.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the universal practice of supplication indicate?
A) That God is merciful
B) That the world is by God's choice
C) That prayer changes nothing
D) That God is compelled to act

Key Takeaway
Universal supplication shows that people intuitively believe God acts by choice, which logically implies He possesses power and will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you raise your hands in supplication, do you truly expect God to respond based on His choice, power, and will? Or do you sometimes pray mechanically, doubting that He can change your situation? Commit to offering one sincere du'a this week with full conviction that God acts by choice and has the power to answer it.
?
This lesson argues that universal supplication proves God's attributes. Think of a time you desperately prayed for something. Did your prayer reveal a deep belief that God could choose to help you? How does that belief shape your daily reliance on Him? Write a short resolution to turn to God first in every difficulty, not as a last resort.

Proof of God's Knowledge from Order and Design
Maturidi presents three arguments for God's knowledge: from continuity of action, from creation of substances with their needs, and from the evidential design of creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the continuity, order, and purposeful design in creation to prove that God possesses knowledge.

Core Idea
Perfect order in creation proves that God acts with knowledge, not ignorance.

Maturidi now turns to the intricate order in creation to establish God's knowledge. He argues that the continuous, well-sequenced actions in the world—and the fact that each thing is created with what sustains it—cannot be the product of an ignorant agent. Moreover, the very fact that creation points to its own createdness and to the oneness of its Creator presupposes knowledge. This lesson explains these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on continuity and order
Read the Arabic and translation about the 'تواصل الفعل' and its perfect sequence.
Notice the phrase 'محكما هو الدليل أنه كان فعله على العلم به'.
2
Analyse the argument from substances
Maturidi mentions that God created substances that are not tested and everything intended for permanence with its sustainment. This shows knowledge of each thing's needs.
Consider how a builder knows which materials and supports are needed.
3
Understand the argument from creation's evidential structure
God created creatures in a way that indicates their origination and their Creator oneness. This could not happen without knowledge.
This is a fine-tuning argument.

?

?

Analogical Reasoning from the Witnessed to the Unseen
Maturidi presents an analogical argument from the witnessed to the unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the analogy between the witnessed world and the unseen to establish that God must have action and speech.

Core Idea
What is true of perfect beings in creation is true of the Creator.

Maturidi begins by inviting us to observe the world around us. In the witnessed realm, any being that is capable and unhindered inevitably performs actions and speech. This observable fact serves as the basis for reasoning about the unseen Creator. If God is capable and not prevented, then He too must possess action and speech. This lesson unpacks that logical step.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully, noting the structure: premise about the witnessed, conclusion about the unseen.
2
Identify the key terms
Pay attention to 'shāhid' (witnessed) and 'ghāʾib' (unseen), and note how 'qādir' (capable) is used.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this argument is foundational: it shows that God is not passive but has actual attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك لا يوجد في الشاهد قادر غير ممنوع لا فعل له، وقادر على الكلام لا كلام له، والشاهد هو دليل الغائب، فلزم ذلك فيه، وبالله التوفيق. ما قد يوصف الخلق بالفساد والشر والقبح والسوء، فلو كان لذاته فعل الله لكان بذلك كله موصوفاً مسمى، فيقال: مفسد شرير قبيح الفعل سيء العمل، فإذا كان الوصف بهذا والتسمية كفراً، ثبت أن الذي به ووصف هو غير هذا، وبالله النجاة. على ذلك الولاد، والطاعة والمعصية، والكسب، لو كان في الحقيقة له لسمي به، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And likewise, there does not exist in the witnessed realm a capable being who is not prevented and has no action, nor a capable speaker who has no speech; and the witnessed realm is the evidence for the unseen, so that is incumbent upon Him. And creation may be described with corruption, evil, ugliness, and badness. If that were essentially the act of God, He would be described and named by all that, and it would be said: 'Corrupter, evil, ugly in action, bad in work.' Since describing and naming with this is unbelief, it is established that the one by whom that is described is other than He. And on that [basis] are birth, obedience and disobedience, and acquisition; if they were in reality from Him, He would be named by them.
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage presents two arguments. First, using the method of analogy from the witnessed (shāhid) to the unseen (ghāʾib): in the physical world, every capable being that is not prevented actually performs actions and speech; therefore, God, who is capable, must also have action and speech. Second, Maturidi argues that evil cannot be attributed to God. Creation includes corruption, evil, ugliness, and badness. If these were essentially God's actions (li-dhātihi fiʿl Allāh), then God would be described as a corrupter, evil, etc. Since such descriptions are blasphemous (kufr), it follows that these actions belong to something other than God. He then extends this to birth, obedience and disobedience, and acquisition (kasb): these, if truly from God, would imply a name for God that is not used, so they cannot be directly from Him. This preserves divine transcendence.

Key Terms
الشاهد
الغائب
القادر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this analogy implies God is like created beings in essence.
Correction: Maturidi is using analogy based on shared logical categories, not anthropomorphism. The analogy highlights that perfect capability entails action, without comparing essences.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why must God have action and speech?
A) Because He is capable and not prevented, just like in the witnessed realm
B) Because scripture says so
C) Because He is all-powerful
D) Because He created the world

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's analogy from the witnessed to the unseen proves that God must have actual attributes of action and speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that God's capability is never prevented, why do you sometimes act as if your problems are too big for Him to solve? What concrete step will you take this week to trust in His unhindered power?
?
The passage argues that a capable speaker must have speech. God has spoken to you through the Quran. When was the last time you listened to His speech as if it were being addressed directly to you, and what change did it make in your life?
?
If the witnessed realm points to the unseen, what does the order and perfection of creation tell you about the God you are accountable to? Are you living as if that God is truly present and active, or do you treat Him as distant and silent?

The Impossibility of Attributing Evil to God
Maturidi refutes attributing evil to God using a conditional argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that evil and corruption cannot be God's essential acts because naming Him with such qualities would be blasphemy.

Core Idea
God is too transcendent to be named with evil.

If God were the direct author of evil, the logical consequence would be that He could be described as 'corrupter' or 'evil'. But such descriptions are clearly unbelief (kufr). Therefore, Maturidi concludes that these acts must originate from something other than God's essence—namely, human acquisition (kasb) or natural processes. This lesson examines the reasoning and its implications for divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Follow Maturidi's conditional: if evil were God's act, then God would be named with evil attributes.
2
Identify the blasphemy
Note that describing God as 'corrupter, evil' is kufr; this establishes that such acts are not from Him.
3
Extend to other categories
See how Maturidi applies the same logic to birth, obedience/disobedience, and acquisition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك لا يوجد في الشاهد قادر غير ممنوع لا فعل له، وقادر على الكلام لا كلام له، والشاهد هو دليل الغائب، فلزم ذلك فيه، وبالله التوفيق. ما قد يوصف الخلق بالفساد والشر والقبح والسوء، فلو كان لذاته فعل الله لكان بذلك كله موصوفاً مسمى، فيقال: مفسد شرير قبيح الفعل سيء العمل، فإذا كان الوصف بهذا والتسمية كفراً، ثبت أن الذي به ووصف هو غير هذا، وبالله النجاة. على ذلك الولاد، والطاعة والمعصية، والكسب، لو كان في الحقيقة له لسمي به، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And likewise, there does not exist in the witnessed realm a capable being who is not prevented and has no action, nor a capable speaker who has no speech; and the witnessed realm is the evidence for the unseen, so that is incumbent upon Him. And creation may be described with corruption, evil, ugliness, and badness. If that were essentially the act of God, He would be described and named by all that, and it would be said: 'Corrupter, evil, ugly in action, bad in work.' Since describing and naming with this is unbelief, it is established that the one by whom that is described is other than He. And on that [basis] are birth, obedience and disobedience, and acquisition; if they were in reality from Him, He would be named by them.
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage presents two arguments. First, using the method of analogy from the witnessed (shāhid) to the unseen (ghāʾib): in the physical world, every capable being that is not prevented actually performs actions and speech; therefore, God, who is capable, must also have action and speech. Second, Maturidi argues that evil cannot be attributed to God. Creation includes corruption, evil, ugliness, and badness. If these were essentially God's actions (li-dhātihi fiʿl Allāh), then God would be described as a corrupter, evil, etc. Since such descriptions are blasphemous (kufr), it follows that these actions belong to something other than God. He then extends this to birth, obedience and disobedience, and acquisition (kasb): these, if truly from God, would imply a name for God that is not used, so they cannot be directly from Him. This preserves divine transcendence.

Key Terms
الفساد
الشر
الكسب
التسمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Maturidi denies God's involvement in all actions.
Correction: He only denies that evil actions are God's essential act (li-dhātihi), not that God is ultimately sovereign.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that evil cannot be directly attributed to God?
A) Because God is good
B) Because describing God as evil would be blasphemy
C) Because evil does not exist
D) Because nature causes evil

Key Takeaway
Maturidi preserves God's transcendence by denying that evil and corruption are His essential acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face suffering or witness evil, are you quick to question God's goodness or attribute unfairness to Him? What does Maturidi's argument demand you affirm instead? Will you consciously remind yourself that evil is not from God's essence and that He is beyond all imperfection?
?
Have you ever described a situation as 'God's will' in a way that made God seem responsible for something evil or unjust? How does this passage correct that impulse? Commit to speaking about God's will in a way that honors His transcendence and absolves Him of any taint.
?
The passage says if evil were God's act, He would be named 'corrupt, evil, ugly'. Does your heart truly recoil at such descriptions? If not, what does that say about your reverence for God? Ask yourself: am I willing to discipline my tongue and heart to only speak of God with the names He has revealed, and to never blame Him for evil?

The Permissibility of Actions from God
Maturidi argues that God's permission to act cannot arise from His essence, proving He is eternally acting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that God's permission of actions cannot be due to His essence, thus His essence is always acting.

Core Idea
God's permission of actions is not from His essence—He is always acting by essence.

Maturidi begins by examining the logical implications of actions being permitted from God. If originally actions were not permitted from Him but later were permitted, the change must be due to something external, not His essence, because His essence is unchanging. This leads to the conclusion that God is acting from His essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the first part of the passage
Read the Arabic carefully focusing on the logical flow about permission and essence.
Note the conditional structure: 'if not from essence, then from another.'
2
Identify the key terms
Terms like الجواز, الفعل, النفس are central. Understand their meaning in this context.
'Jawāz' here means permissibility, not ability.
3
Follow the argument
Trace the logical deduction: if change cannot be from essence, it must be from external, proving essence is always acting.
Maturidi uses a rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī).
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand why this protects God's unchanging nature while affirming His action.
This is a key point in Maturidi theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً أن الله تعالى إذ لم يجز منه الفعل في الأصل ثم جاز، فإما أن يكون لا يجوز لنفسه، فيجب أن يكون كذلك أبداً، أو لغيره، وهو الذي عنه السؤال، وإذ ثبت أنه لا لنفسه يجوز غير فاعل، فهو لنفسه فاعل، والله الموفق. وقال بعض من يزعم أن الخلق هو فعل الله في الحقيقة إنه كالصلاة وهي فعل لفعله في الحقيقة. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله: وذلك وهم؛ إذ ذلك اسم هو اسم الحقيقة، ثم لم يدل على أن الخلق هو في الحقيقة فعله ليُسَلَّم له. على أنا قد بيَّنا من حق التسمية به ما يبين إحالة ذلك.
And also, that God Almighty, when He did not permit action from Himself originally and then permitted it, it is either that it is not permissible from His essence, in which case it must be so forever, or from another, which is the question at hand. And when it is established that it is not from His essence that it is permissible for Him to be non-acting, then from His essence He is acting. And some of those who claim that creation is the act of God in reality said that it is like prayer, which is an act for His act in reality. Abu Mansur—may God have mercy on him—said: That is a delusion, because that name is a name of reality, yet it does not indicate that creation is in reality His act, so that it could be conceded to him. Indeed, we have already explained from the right of naming by it what clarifies the impossibility of that.
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage deals with two issues. First, Maturidi argues about God's permission of actions: originally, actions were not permitted from God (i.e., they were not part of His eternal essence), but later actions become possible. This change cannot be due to God's essence (because that would imply change in God), so it must be due to something external (the creation of actions). Since it is established that it is not due to His essence that He is ever non-acting, then from His essence He is always acting. Second, he refutes an objection: someone claims that creation is God's act in reality (fiʿl Allāh fī al-ḥaqīqa), comparing it to prayer being an act of God. Maturidi rejects this as a delusion (wahm). While 'creation' is a real name, it does not follow that creation is God's real act in that sense; the rival's analogy fails because prayer is not called 'God's act' literally. He cites earlier arguments about naming to show its impossibility.

Key Terms
الفعل
الجواز
النفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think God's permission to act indicates a change in His essence.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that the change is due to external factors, not a change in God's eternal essence.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why cannot the permission of actions be from God's essence?
A) Because God's essence is eternal and unchanging
B) Because actions are created
C) Because God is not an agent
D) Because the Quran says so

Key Takeaway
God's essence is inherently acting; any change in the permissibility of actions is due to external factors, not a change in God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's essence is always acting, without pause or change, then your very existence at this moment is a direct act of His essence. Do you live with the constant awareness that you are being created anew every instant? What would change in your prayer or gratitude if you truly felt this? Commit to one action today that acknowledges His continuous creation.
?
The lesson teaches that God's permission to act comes from outside His essence, not from a change in Him. How often do you blame God for changes in your life, forgetting that He does not change? Can you identify a specific trial you attributed to God's 'turning away'—and instead reframe it as a call to return to the One who never ceases acting? Write down that trial and a new perspective.
?
Maturidi argues that God is necessarily acting (fāʿil bi-dhātihī). This means His action is not a choice He makes after being inactive. If God's very essence is action, then your existence is not a result of a long-ago decision but an ongoing necessity from Him. How would it change your feeling of security or desperation if you truly believed that God cannot stop acting toward you? Take a moment to tell God directly how this makes you feel, and ask Him to increase your certainty.

Refuting the Analogy of Prayer for Creation
Maturidi refutes the analogy comparing creation to prayer as God's real act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the claim that creation is God's act in reality, based on the analogy of prayer.

Core Idea
The name 'creation' does not prove it is God's real act as claimed.

Some opponents argued that creation is God's act in reality (fiʿl Allāh fī al-ḥaqīqa), comparing it to prayer being an act of God. Maturidi exposes this as a delusion, showing that the name 'creation' alone does not demonstrate the claimed reality, and his earlier discussion on naming already refuted this.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Focus on the rival's claim and Maturidi's response.
The rival uses an analogy with prayer.
2
Identify the rival's analogy
They claim creation is like prayer, which they consider an act for God's act in reality.
This is a Mu'tazili-like view.
3
Understand Maturidi's refutation
He calls it a delusion; the name does not prove the reality; he refers to earlier arguments.
The name 'creation' is a real name, but not proof of the claimed theological reality.
4
Connect to broader theology
This protects the distinction between God's eternal attributes and temporal acts.
Maturidi's method uses linguistic analysis.

God Must Have an Act: The Argument from the Witness
Maturidi uses witnessed-world analogy to establish God's necessary act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses analogy from the witnessed world to prove that God necessarily has an act.

Core Idea
A capable being not prevented must act; God is that being.

Maturidi begins with a simple observation: in our experienced world, any capable being who is not prevented from acting does act. This rule from the witnessed world is then applied to God, who is the Unseen. The passage establishes a foundational principle for subsequent arguments about God's attributes and acts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the structure: premise from the witnessed world, then application to the unseen.
The phrase 'al-shahid huwa dalil al-gha'ib' is a key methodological principle in kalam.
2
Identify the logical structure
The author presents two conditional situations: a capable being not prevented must have an act; a being capable of speech not prevented must have speech. Generalize the principle.
3
Apply the analogy to God
Since God is the ultimate capable being and is not prevented, He must have an act. Ask: what is that act? The commentary hints it is creation.
This argument does not specify the act but establishes that God is necessarily an agent.
4
Reflect on the method
Understand that this is qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid – inferring the unseen from the witnessed. This method is central to Maturidi's theology.
Consider how this differs from other theological approaches.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كذلك لا يوجد في الشاهد قادر غير ممنوع لا فعل له، وقادر على الكلام منع لا كلام له، والشاهد هو دليل الغائب، فلزم ذلك فيه، وبالله التوفيق. ما قد يوصف الخلق بالفساد والشر والقبح والسوء، فلو كان لذاته فعل الله لكان بذلك كله موصوفا مسمى، فيقال: مفسد شرير قبيح الفعل سيء العمل، فإذا كان الوصف بهذا والتسمية كفرا، ثبت أن الذي به ووصف هو غير هذا، وبالله النجاة، على ذلك الولاد، والطاعة والمعصية، والكسب، لو كان في الحقيقة له لسمى به، ولا قوة إلا بالله
Likewise, there is not found in the witnessed world a capable being who is not prevented from acting without an act, nor a capable being of speech who is prevented without speech. And the witnessed is the evidence for the unseen; so that rule applies to Him. And with Allah is success. As for what is described in creation of corruption, evil, ugliness, and badness, if it were by His essence the act of Allah, then He would be described and named by all of that. It would be said: corrupt, evil, ugly in action, bad in deed. And since description and naming with this is disbelief, it is established that that by which creation is described is other than this. And with Allah is deliverance. Similarly, birth, obedience, disobedience, and acquisition—if they were in reality His, He would be named by them. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage is an argument from analogy (qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid) combined with a reductio ad absurdum. It begins by establishing a principle from the witnessed world: any capable being (qadir) who is not prevented from acting necessarily has an act; similarly, a being capable of speech who is not prevented necessarily has speech. Since God is the Unseen (gha'ib), this rule applies to Him by analogy, implying that God must have an act (fi'l) and specifically the act of creation. The passage then presents a second argument: if the act of creation were identical with God's essence (dhat), then since created things are described with corruption, evil, ugliness, and badness, God would be described and named with these same qualities. But describing God as 'corrupt', 'evil', etc., is disbelief (kufr). Therefore, the act of creation is not identical with God's essence; rather, it is distinct. The same reasoning applies to other events like birth, obedience, disobedience, and kasb (acquisition) — if they were God's acts in reality, He would be named accordingly, which is not the case. The passage concludes by affirming divine transcendence above such defects.

Key Terms
الشاهد (al-shahid)
الغائب (al-gha'ib)
القادر (al-qadir)
الفعل (al-fi'l)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God does not act or that His essence alone suffices without an act.
Correction: This argument shows that God, as an omnipotent being not prevented, necessarily has an act, implying He is an agent.

Checkpoint
What is the conclusion Maturidi draws from the fact that a capable being in the witnessed world always has an act?
A) The witnessed world is evidence for the unseen
B) God must have an act
C) God is the only capable being
D) Creation is eternal

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that God, as a capable being without prevention, necessarily has an act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God necessarily has an act, and your existence is part of that act, what does that mean for how you live this day? Will you live as if you are a passive occurrence or an intentional act of God?
?
The argument relies on observing that a capable being not prevented must act. Where in your own life have you seen God's act? And if He is necessarily active, why do you sometimes live as if He is distant or uninvolved?
?
You have learned that the witnessed world points to the unseen. In what specific area of your life are you ignoring the evidence of God's act? What will you do today to align with that reality?

Creation Is Not God's Essence: Argument from Imperfection
Maturidi argues that creation's imperfections prove it is not God's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that creation cannot be identical with God's essence because that would attribute imperfection to God.

Core Idea
If creation were God's essence, He would be called corrupt and evil that is impossible.

Maturidi presents a powerful reductio argument: if the act of creation were identical with God's essence, then since creation contains corruption, evil, ugliness, and badness, God would be described by those names. But calling God 'corrupt' or 'evil' is disbelief. Therefore, creation is distinct from God's essence, affirming divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the hypothetical
The passage begins with a conditional: 'if it were by His essence the act of Allah...' Understand the scenario and its consequences.
The key phrase 'law kana li-dhatihi fi'lu Allah' means 'if the act of Allah were by His essence.'
2
List the descriptions of creation mentioned
Creation is described with corruption (fasad), evil (sharr), ugliness (qubh), and badness (su'). Notice these are negative attributes.
3
Follow the reductio
If creation were identical with God's essence, then God would be described by those negative attributes. That would lead to naming Him with them, which is kufr.
The passage explicitly states that such naming is kufr.
4
Understand the conclusion
Since describing God with these is impossible (kufr), creation must be distinct from God's essence. The same reasoning applies to birth, obedience, disobedience, and kasb.
These additional examples reinforce the argument.

It begins by establishing a principle from the witnessed world: any capable being (qadir) who is not prevented from acting necessarily has an act; similarly, a being capable of speech who is not prevented necessarily has speech. ?

The Modal Argument for God Being an Agent by Essence
Maturidi proves that God is essentially an agent via modal reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's modal argument that God is an agent by essence, not by acquisition of the attribute of action.

Core Idea
God's agency is essential, not acquired; action is possible because His essence does not prevent it.

Maturidi presents a crisp logical argument to establish that God is an agent by His very essence. He considers a hypothetical scenario and eliminates possibilities to reach a necessary conclusion. This lesson unpacks that argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the literal translation. Pay attention to the conditional structure.
Notice the phrase 'يجز منه' – the OCR suggests a possible duplication, but the meaning is clear.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The passage presents two options for why action might originally be impossible for God: due to His essence or due to something else. Find these in the text.
The phrase 'فإما أن يكون لا يجوز لنفسه، أو لغيره' marks the disjunction.
3
Understand elimination of the first possibility
If the impossibility were due to God's essence, it would be eternal. But we observe that action is possible (since existence is actual). So the first option is impossible.
The conclusion 'يجوز غير فاعل' is key – it establishes that He is not prevented from being non-acting by His essence.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Having eliminated the first possibility, it follows that God is an agent by essence, not by acquisition. The argument is complete.
The final phrase 'فهو لنفسه فاعل' directly states the conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن الله تعالى إذ لم يجز منه يجز منه الفعل في الأصل ثم جاز، فإما أن يكون لا يجوز لنفسه، فيجب أن يكون كذلك أبدا، أو لغيره، وهو الذي عنه السؤال، وإذ ثبت أنه لا لنفسه يجوز غير فاعل، فهو لنفسه فاعل، والله الموفق
And also, [when] Allah Almighty—if action in the beginning was not permissible for Him, then [later] became permissible—then either it is not permissible due to His essence, in which case it must be so forever, or [it is not permissible] due to something else, which is the subject of inquiry. And when it is established that it is not due to His essence that He is permitted to be non-acting, then He is an agent due to His essence. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage presents a modal argument about the possibility of God's action. It considers a hypothetical: if action were originally impossible for God and then became possible, what is the reason? Two possibilities: (1) the impossibility was due to God's essence (dhat), in which case it would be eternally impossible, or (2) it was due to something external. Since we observe that action is possible for God, the impossibility cannot be due to His essence; therefore, it must have been due to something else. From this it follows that God's essence does not preclude action, meaning that He is an agent (fa'il) by essence. The argument guards against the idea that God acquires the attribute of agency at a certain time, affirming that agency is essential to God.

Key Terms
الجواز (al-jawaz)
الذات (al-dhat)
الفعل (al-fi'l)
الفاعل (al-fa'il)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's attribute of agency is acquired at creation, i.e., He was not an agent before creating.
Correction: Maturidi argues that if agency were acquired, then originally action would have been impossible for God. But that impossibility cannot be due to His essence, because then it would be eternal. Since action is possible, agency must be essential, not acquired.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi conclude from the possibility of God's action?
A) That God's action is possible only after creation.
B) That God's essence does not prevent action, so He is an agent by essence.
C) That action is impossible for God in essence.
D) That God's agency is acquired from an external source.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi proves that God's essence does not preclude action, so He is an agent by essence, not by acquisition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's essence does not prevent action, why do you sometimes live as though He is distant or inactive? How does this truth change your expectation of His response to your du'a today?
?
This argument shows that God's agency flows from His very nature—He is always capable of acting. What area of your life are you waiting for God to 'change' before He can act? How will you trust in His essential agency starting now?
?
The argument forces you to choose: either God's essence prevents action (making Him eternally inactive) or He is an agent by essence. Have you ever acted as if God were powerless in a situation? What would it mean for you to truly believe that His essence is inherently active, not passive?

Why Eternal Takwin Does Not Imply an Eternal Mukawwan
Maturidi answers the objection that if takwin is eternal, the mukawwan must also be eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the eternity of the attribute of takwin does not necessitate the eternity of its effect, the mukawwan.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes produce temporal effects at their appointed times.

In this passage, Maturidi addresses a common objection: if Allah is eternally described as 'the Bringer into Existence,' then the things He brings into existence must also be eternal. To answer, he draws a parallel between takwin and other divine attributes like power, will, and knowledge, which are eternal yet their objects are temporal. This distinction is crucial for preserving both God's eternal perfection and the temporal nature of creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to see the structure: first the objection, then Maturidi's answer. Notice how he sets up the analogy.
The objection is in the first sentence: 'For if it is said...'
2
Understand the analogy with other attributes
Maturidi compares takwin to power, will, and knowledge. These are eternal attributes, yet their objects (the things known, willed, etc.) are temporal. Understand why this analogy works.
The key phrase: 'takwin is like the statement about power over things, will for them, and knowledge of them.'
3
Grasp the principle and proofs
Identify the two proofs Maturidi gives: (1) God was described with takwin before any creation, and (2) if the time of the effect is not mentioned, it would imply eternity or ignorance. Consider how these support the distinction between attribute and object.
The example of the Hour is used to illustrate the second proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: إذ وصف الله بالتكوين في الأزل لم لا كان المكون؟ قيل: كون ليكون الأشياء على ما تكون، وذلك نحو القول بالقدرة على الأشياء والإرادة لها والعلم بها ليكون كل شيء في وقته، والحدث على الذي يكون لا على من بعد - في حد الكائن من غير به، وإن كان الذي يكون العليم به والقدرة عليه. تغير العلم والأصل أن الله تعالى إذا أطلق الوصف له، وصف بما يوصف من الفعل والعلم ونحوه، يلزم الوصف به في الأزل. وإذا ذكر معه الذي هو تحت وصفه به من المعلوم والمقدور عليه والمراد والمكون يذكر فيه أوقات تلك الأشياء لئلا يتوهم قدم تلك الأشياء، ولا قوة إلا بالله. دليل الأول: ما سبق له الوصف، ودليل الثاني: أنه إذا لم يذكر وقت المفعول به يومي قدم المفعول أو الجهل به في غير وقته، وكذلك العجز؛ لأنه إذا قيل: مكون للساعة يومي أنه كون ليكون في هذه الساعة، وكذلك العلم والقدرة عليه والإرادة، ولا قوة إلا بالله
For if it is said: Since Allah is described with takwin (bringing into existence) in pre-eternity, why is the thing brought into existence (mukawwan) not [eternal]? It is said: [Takwin is] 'being (kawn) in order that things be' as they are, and that is like the statement about power over things, will for them, and knowledge of them, so that everything occurs at its time. And the event is according to what occurs, not due to any after... [some phrases unclear]. Knowledge does not change, and the principle is that when Allah is described absolutely with an attribute, He is described with it in pre-eternity. And when the object of that attribute (the known, the willed, the brought into existence) is mentioned, the times of those things are mentioned so that they are not imagined to be eternal. And there is no power except with Allah. The proof of the first [point] is that He was described with it before [the thing existed]. The proof of the second is that if the time of the effect is not mentioned, it would imply the eternity of the effect or ignorance of it at its proper time, and likewise impotence. Because if it is said: 'Bringer into existence of the Hour,' it implies that He brings it into existence to be at this hour. Similarly for knowledge, power, and will.
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer about the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The objector says: if God is described with takwin from pre-eternity (azal), then why is the thing brought into existence (mukawwan) not also eternal? Maturidi's answer: takwin is like power (qudra), will (irada), and knowledge ('ilm). These attributes are eternal, but their objects are temporal and occur at their appointed times. For example, God's power is eternal even though the things powered occur at specific times. Similarly, takwin is 'being (kawn) for the purpose that things be' at their proper times. Maturidi then states a principle: when an absolute description is given to God, it applies in pre-eternity; but when the object of that description is mentioned, one must also mention its time to avoid the false notion that the object itself is eternal. He provides two proofs: (1) God was described with takwin before any creation existed; (2) if the time of the effect is not specified, it might be imagined that the effect is eternal or that God is ignorant of its proper time, which would imply impotence. The example of 'Bringer into existence of the Hour' illustrates: it implies that the Hour is brought into existence at a specific future time, not eternally. Thus, takwin is an eternal attribute whose effect is temporal.

Key Terms
التكوين (al-takwin)
المكون (al-mukawwan)
الأزل (al-azal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An eternal cause must have an eternal effect.
Correction: Maturidi shows that eternal attributes like takwin produce temporal effects at their appointed times, just as power and will do.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does eternal takwin not require the mukawwan to be eternal?
A) Because takwin is not a real attribute.
B) Because the effect is not produced by takwin but by something else.
C) Because takwin is like power and will, which are eternal but produce temporal effects.
D) Because the mukawwan exists before takwin.

Key Takeaway
Takwin is an eternal attribute that brings things into existence at their appointed times, not eternally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe that Allah's attribute of creation is eternal, yet you sometimes feel that your own existence is the result of random chance. How does knowing that the attribute of takwin is eternal but its effect is timed specifically for your existence change the way you view your purpose? What action will you take today to align your life with that purpose?
?
If you truly understood that Allah's power, knowledge, and will are eternal and that their objects come into being at their appointed times, would you worry less about the future? What specific worry can you release right now based on this lesson?
?
The lesson says that if the time of the effect were not mentioned, it would imply impotence or ignorance. Do you ever act as if God is ignorant of the right time for things to happen in your life? In what area of your life are you trying to force God's timing, and how will you submit to His appointed time?

The Timing of Divine Takwin: Why No Immediate Creation Does Not Imply Impotence
Maturidi answers that takwin is for a future time, not immediate, so impotence does not apply.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) is directed toward a specific future time, and that the absence of an immediate created thing does not indicate any deficiency in God's power.

Core Idea
Takwin is for a specific future time, not immediate existence, so no impotence arises.

Imam Maturidi now addresses a subtle objection: if God has the attribute of takwin (the power to bring things into existence), but at a given moment no thing is actually being created, does that not suggest impotence? After all, if a person claims to be able to create but creates nothing, we doubt their power. Maturidi clarifies that the divine takwin is directed toward a specific future moment when the created thing will appear. The attribute itself is eternal, but its effect occurs at its appointed time. This reasoning also applies to other attributes like will, knowledge, hearing, and seeing.

Guided Path
1
Read the Objection and Response
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the overall structure: an objection followed by Maturidi's answer.
Pay attention to the conditional phrase 'if it were... then...'.
2
Understand the Conditional Condition
Notice that Maturidi says impotence would only apply if takwin were for immediate existence (being for a time) and nothing occurred. He contrasts this with takwin being for a future time.
3
Apply the Same Logic to Other Attributes
See how Maturidi extends the reasoning to will (irada), knowledge ('ilm), hearing (sam'), seeing (basr), generosity (karm), and bounty (jud). All are eternal but their objects are temporal.
This shows a consistent principle.
4
Reflect on the Principle
Conclude that the temporality of the object does not affect the eternity or perfection of the attribute. This defends divine power against the objection.
The key is the appointed time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: في التكوين ولا مكون إثبات العجز؟ قيل: إنما يكون ذلك لو كان التكوين الكون لوق فلم يكن، وكذلك في الإرادة والعلم به إذا لم يكن جهل واضطرار، فأما ليكون للوقت الذي يكون فيه فلا، العلم، وعلى ذلك السمع والبصر والكرم والجود، إنه على ما بينا من موصوف بها في الأزل وإن كان ما يسمع ويبصر وما ذكر حادث، وعلى ذلك جري الحدود، ولا بد من ذكر الوقت للمسموع عند ذكر الأمرين، فمثله الأول، ولا قوه إلا بالله
For if it is said: In takwin without a thing brought into existence (mukan) there is an affirmation of impotence? It is said: That would only be the case if takwin were 'being' for a time and it did not occur. Similarly for will and knowledge, if there is no ignorance and necessity. But for it to be for the time at which it occurs, then no. And similarly for hearing, seeing, generosity, and bounty; He is described with them in pre-eternity, even though what is heard and seen and mentioned are temporal. And on that runs the occurrence of events. And it is necessary to mention the time for the heard when mentioning the two matters. So like the first. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage answers a further objection: if takwin is an attribute of God but no thing is actually brought into existence (i.e., no mukan exists at a given moment), does that not indicate impotence (ajz) in God? Maturidi responds by distinguishing the purpose of takwin. He says that if takwin were intended to produce immediate existence (being for an immediate time) and nothing occurred, that would indeed be impotence. But takwin is directed toward existence at a specific future time. Similarly, the will (irada) and knowledge ('ilm) do not demand immediate occurrence; they are for their proper times. The same applies to attributes like hearing (sam'), seeing (basr), generosity (karm), and bounty (jud). These attributes are eternal, but their objects (what is heard, seen, etc.) are temporal. The temporality of the objects does not imply a defect in the eternal attribute. Maturidi concludes that the rule is the same: the time of the object must be mentioned when speaking of the attribute, to avoid confusion. Thus, takwin without an immediate mukan is not a sign of impotence but of the attribute's orientation toward a future time.

Key Terms
العجز
التكوين
المكون
الإرادة
العلم
السمع
البصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God has the attribute of takwin but no creation is currently occurring, that suggests He is unable to create.
Correction: Maturidi explains that takwin is directed toward a specific future time, so the absence of an immediate created thing does not indicate impotence.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, when would takwin without a mukan indicate impotence?
A) If takwin were intended to produce immediate existence and nothing occurred.
B) If takwin is an eternal attribute.
C) If the mukan exists eventually.
D) If God has will and knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's key insight is that divine attributes like takwin are eternal and oriented toward specific future times; the absence of an immediate effect does not indicate any deficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a situation in your life where you have been waiting for God's help to manifest. Does this lesson challenge your impatience? How can you sincerely adopt the belief that God's takwin is at work even when you see no change?
?
Consider an area where you have doubted God's power because your prayers seemed unanswered. Based on Maturidi's argument, what is the flaw in expecting immediate results? What would it take to truly trust His timing?
?

Why Takwin in Eternity Does Not Imply Eternal Creation
Maturidi answers the objection that takwin in pre-eternity implies the eternity of the created thing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why describing Allah with takwin (bringing into existence) in pre-eternity does not necessitate the eternal existence of the created thing.

Core Idea
Takwin is eternal, but its objects are temporal.

A common objection against the attribute of takwin is that if God is described as 'the Bringer into Existence' in pre-eternity, then the thing brought into existence must also be eternal. Imam Maturidi addresses this objection with a precise theological distinction, using the nature of power, will, and knowledge as parallels. In this passage, you will read his answer and the two proofs that support it.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Pay close attention to how Maturidi responds to the challenge. Notice that he does not deny takwin's eternity but reinterprets its reference to the temporal existence of its objects.
The answer uses the phrase 'كون ليكون' which is key.
2
Understand the analogy
Maturidi equates takwin with power (qudra), will (irada), and knowledge (ilm). These attributes are eternal, yet their objects are temporal. Ask yourself: how does this analogy refute the objection?
The analogy shows that an eternal attribute does not imply an eternal object.
3
Grasp the general principle
Maturidi states a principle: when God is described with an attribute (act, knowledge, etc.), that description is necessarily eternal. However, when the object of that attribute is mentioned, its time must be specified to avoid imagining that the object itself is eternal.
This principle is crucial for understanding how to speak about God's attributes without implying creation's eternity.
4
Study the two proofs
The first proof is that the prior description of God (the attribute) is eternal. The second proof: if the time of the object is not mentioned, it could imply either that the object is eternal or that God is ignorant of its proper time. Reflect on why this is a problem.
The second proof is illustrated with the example of the Hour.
5
Reflect on the example
Consider the statement 'Maker of the Hour'. If unspecified, it might imply the Hour is eternal or that God's making is tied to a specific time in a limiting way. Maturidi shows that specifying time preserves correct belief.
This example helps solidify the second proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : إذ وصف الله بالتكوين في الأزل لم لا كان المكون ؟ قيل : كون ليكون الأشياء على ما تكون ، وذلك نحو القول بالقدرة على الأشياء والإرادة لها والعلم بها ليكون كل شيء في وقته ، والحدث على الذي يكون لا على من بعد - في حد الكائن من غير به ، وإن كان الذي يكون العليم اعلم به والقدرة عليه. تغير العلم والأصل أن الله تعالى إذا أطلق الوصف له ، وصف بما يوصف من الفعل والعلم ونحوه ، يلزم الوصف به في الأزل . وإذا ذكر معه الذي هو تحت وصفه به من المعلوم والمقدور عليه والمراد والمكون يذكر فيه أوقات تلك الأشياء لئلا يتوهم قدم تلك الأشياء ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . دليل الأول، ما سبق له الوصف ، ودليل الثانى أنه إذا لم يذكر وقت المفعول به يومى قدم المفعول أو الجهل به في غير وقته ، وكذلك العجز ؛ لأنه إذا قيل : مكون للساعة يومى أنه كون ليكون في هذه الساعة أنه كون ليكون في هذه الساعة ، وكذلك العلم والقدرة عليه والإرادة ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
If it is said: When God is described with takwin (bringing into existence) in pre-eternity, why is the created thing (mukawwan) not [eternal]? It is said: [He is] the One who causes to be (kawn) so that things come to be as they are, and this is like the statement about power over things, will for them, and knowledge of them, so that each thing is in its time, and the occurrence is upon what occurs, not upon what is after – in the limit of the existent from non-existence, even if the one who is, the Knower, is more knowing of it and has power over it. The clarification of knowledge and the principle is that when God, exalted, is absolutely described with description, He is described with what is described of act and knowledge and the like, the description of it in pre-eternity is necessary. And when what is under His description is mentioned, of the known, the predetermined, the willed, and the brought into existence, the times of those things are mentioned in it lest the pre-eternity of those things be imagined. And there is no power except with God. The first proof: what preceded for Him the description. And the second proof: that if the time of the object of the act is not mentioned, it implies pre-eternity of the object or ignorance of it in other than its time, and likewise incapability; because if it is said: 'Maker of the Hour', it implies that He causes it to be in this hour, that He causes it to be in this hour. And likewise knowledge, power over it, and will. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by two supporting proofs. The objection states that if God is described with the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) in pre-eternity (al-azal), then the created thing (mukawwan) must also be eternal, since the attribute is eternal. Maturidi answers by explaining that takwin is like power (qudra), will (irada), and knowledge (ilm): it is for things to come into existence at their proper times. The attribute itself is eternal, but its object is temporal. He then states a general principle: when God is described with an attribute (like act, knowledge, etc.), that description necessarily applies in pre-eternity. However, when the object of that attribute (the known, the predetermined, the willed, the created) is mentioned, its time must be specified to avoid the false notion that the object itself is eternal. Then he gives two proofs: first, the prior description of God (that He is described with the attribute in eternity); second, that if the time of the object is not mentioned, it could imply either that the object is eternal or that God is ignorant of its proper time. He illustrates with the example of the Hour: if one says 'Maker of the Hour' without specifying, it could imply that the Hour is eternal or that God's act of making is tied to this hour in a way that suggests limitation. Thus, specifying time is necessary to avoid misunderstanding.

Key Terms
التكوين
المكون
الأزل
القدرة
الإرادة
العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That describing God with takwin in pre-eternity necessarily implies the eternal existence of the created thing.
Correction: Takwin is an eternal attribute, but its object is brought into existence at its appointed time, just as power, will, and knowledge are eternal but their objects are temporal.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's response, why does describing God with takwin (bringing into existence) in pre-eternity not imply that the created thing (mukawwan) is eternal?
A) Because takwin is identical to power and will, and power and will are not restricted to specific times.
B) Because takwin is only for things that will exist at specific times, and mentioning the time of the created thing prevents the assumption of its pre-eternity.
C) Because the object of takwin is non-existent, so it cannot be eternal.
D) Because God's attributes are not real descriptions but mere metaphors.

Key Takeaway
Takwin is an eternal attribute of God that brings things into existence at their appointed times, and the temporal nature of its objects does not compromise the eternality of the attribute.

?

Refuting the Claim of Incapability in Takwin
Maturidi refutes the objection using time-bound vs. time-neutral attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the distinction between time-bound and time-neutral attributes to refute the objection that takwin without a simultaneous created thing indicates incapability.

Core Idea
Takwin does not require a simultaneous created thing to be real.

Maturidi answers a common objection: if God 'brings into existence' without a thing being created at that moment, doesn't that show weakness? He distinguishes between attributes tied to a specific time and those that are eternal. This passage uses that distinction to defend God's power.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the objector's claim and Maturidi's immediate response.
The objector says takwin without mukawwan indicates incapability.
2
Identify the condition for validity
Find where Maturidi specifies the condition under which the objection would hold. He says it would only be valid if takwin were for a specific time and the thing did not occur.
God's takwin is for the ordained time, not a past time.
3
Observe the extension to other attributes
Notice that Maturidi extends the same reasoning to will, knowledge, hearing, sight, generosity, and bounty. These attributes are eternal even though their objects are temporal.
This reinforces the principle of time-neutral attributes.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Reflect on the principle: an attribute can be eternal and perfect even if its effect appears in time. Temporality of the object does not imply imperfection in the attribute.
This safeguards God's transcendence and capability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : في التكوين ولا مكون إثبات العجز قيل : إنما يكون ذلك لو كان التكوين الكون لوق فلم يكن ، وكذلك في الإرادة والعلم به إذا لم يكن جهل واضطرار ، فأما ليكون للوقت الذي يكون فيه فلا ، العلم، وعلى ذلك السمع والبصر والكرم والجود ، إنه على ما بينا من موصوف بها في الأزل وإن كان ما يسمع ويبصر وما ذكر حادث ، وعلى ذلك جري الحدوث ، ولا بد من ذكر الوقت للمسموع عند ذكر الأمرين الأمرين ، فمثله الأول ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
If it is said: [Saying] 'takwin (bringing into existence) without a mukawwan (created thing)' is an affirmation of incapability. It is said: That would only be if takwin were a being (kawn) for a time and it was not. And likewise with will and knowledge of it if there were no ignorance and compulsion. But as for it being for the time in which it will be, then no. [This applies to] hearing, sight, generosity, and bounty: He is described by them in pre-eternity as we have explained, even though what is heard, seen, and mentioned is temporal. Upon that runs temporality. And it is necessary to mention the time of the heard thing when mentioning the two matters. So the like of the first applies. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector claims that saying 'takwin' (bringing into existence) without a simultaneous 'mukawwan' (created thing) proves that God is incapable (al-'ajz). Maturidi answers by specifying the condition under which this claim would hold: it would only be valid if the takwin were for a specific time (kawn li-waqt) and the thing did not occur at that time. But God's takwin is for the time when the thing actually will be created. The same applies to will (irada) and knowledge (ilm): they do not imply ignorance or compulsion. Then Maturidi extends the argument to other attributes like hearing (sam'), sight (basar), generosity (karm), and bounty (jūd). These attributes are described in pre-eternity even though their objects are temporal. The temporality of the objects is part of the nature of creation. When mentioning the attribute, one must mention the time of the sensed object to avoid confusion. This is analogous to the first case of takwin. The underlying principle is that the attribute is eternal, but the object's temporality is indicated by specifying its time.

Key Terms
التكوين
المكون
العجز
السمع
البصر
الكرم
الجود
الحدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The absence of a simultaneous created thing means God's power is incomplete or that He is incapable.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that takwin is an eternal attribute that brings things into existence at their ordained times. The lack of a simultaneous created object does not imply incapability because takwin is not a time-bound action.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, when would the claim that 'takwin without a mukawwan' indicate incapability be valid?
A) When takwin is for a specific time and the thing does not occur at that time.
B) When takwin is eternal and the thing is also eternal.
C) When God does not create anything at all.
D) Always, because an action requires an effect at the same moment.

Key Takeaway
Takwin is an eternal attribute that brings things into being at their ordained times, not a temporal action requiring a simultaneous effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray for something that has not yet happened, do you ever feel that God’s power is somehow not fully engaged until the moment it arrives? How does the teaching that takwin is an eternal attribute—acting precisely when ordained—change your confidence in the effectiveness of your prayers right now?
?
What if your own ‘here and now’ demands for immediate results in your life actually reveal a hidden assumption that God’s attributes are dependent on time? Will you allow this lesson to reshape your patience, or will you continue to measure God’s care by the clock?
?
The passage insists that hearing and sight are described in pre-eternity even though their objects are temporal. Have you ever thought of God as 'waiting to hear' your dua until you speak it? What would it mean to truly believe He has been 'hearing' you from before time, and that your speech merely aligns with His eternal awareness?

The Principle of Greater Perfection: God's Action Extends Beyond the Present
Maturidi states the principle of greater perfection and applies it to God's attribute of takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that God's attribute of takwin is a description of perfection precisely because it is not confined to the moment of the thing's existence.

Core Idea
An action that extends beyond the present proves power, not weakness.

Maturidi begins by establishing a fundamental principle: the one whose action does not go beyond the immediate moment is described with incapability, while the one whose action extends beyond and effects occur at his disposal is described with power. He then applies this to God, showing that God's takwin is perfect because it precedes creation. In this lesson, we will unpack this principle and see how it refutes the objection that takwin without a simultaneous created thing indicates incapability.

Guided Path
1
Read the principle carefully
Read the opening statement about the one who does not go beyond the actual vs. the one who does. Notice the contrast between 'description of incapability' and 'description of power'.
2
Understand the spatial analogy
Maturidi extends the principle to space: the one whose action is confined to his own sphere is inferior to the one whose action reaches all spheres. This reinforces the perfection of God's action.
3
Contrast human and divine action
Human acts are time-bound because of instruments and occupation. God acts by His own essence, timelessly. This shows that takwin is not limited to the moment of creation.
This refutes the objection that takwin must be simultaneous with its effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل أن الذي لا يعدو الواقع يفعله وقت الوصف له بالفعل وصف عجز، والذي يعدوه ويقع عنده وصف قدرة، كمن يكون منه فعل الشيء وضده المتمكن منه أنه أتم من جهة فعله. وكذلك من لا يعد فعله حيزه هو دون من يقع فعله في كل حيز، كذلك وصف الله بالذي ذكرت؛ إذ هو وصف التمام. مع ما لا يقع فعل العبد لغير وقته لأنه عن [شغله؟] بالفعل يكون وبالآلات، والله سبحانه بنفسه يفعل، وذلك كما علم سبحانه بذاته وقدر بذاته، وكل من سواه بغير الذي ذكرت لولا ذلك ما قام به فعل، والله هو ينشئ لا شيء: لذلك بطل التقدير بالذي قالوا. وعلى مثل ما ذكرتُ أمر القدرة والإرادة وجميع ما بينا. ودليل آخر: أنه يوجد من العبد الفعل المتولد، يقع الفراغ بعده بأوقات كالرمي والجنايات، يستحق اسم القاتل والجاني والمصيب بعد انقضاء حقيقة فعله [قبله مستقيم من مستقيم من الله؟]، وإن كان لا يوصف فعله بالطباع والتولد؛ لما أن خروج [أحد؟] الوجهين في الشاهد لم يمنع من تحقيق الفعل، فمثله في الغائب، وإن لم يكن من ذلك الوجه على ما بينا من إثبات شيء ليس بجسم، على جواز القول في الله بالشيء وإن لم يكن عرضا، وكل شيء في الشاهد غير جسم فهو عرض بحق الوجود لا أن ذلك اسمه، فمثله الأول، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وإيضا إن الذي قالوا أمارة العجز، إذ لا يقدر العبد على ما لا يتحقق مفعوله معه، كما لا يقدر عليه دون استعمال نفسه بالتحريك والتسكين، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And the principle is that the one who does not go beyond the actual, doing it at the time of description of him with the act, is a description of incapability; and the one who goes beyond it and it occurs with him is a description of power, like one from whom occurs both the thing and its opposite, [he] being capable of it, that he is more perfect in terms of his act. And likewise, the one whose action does not go beyond his sphere is inferior to the one whose action occurs in every sphere. Thus is the description of God with what I have mentioned; for it is the description of perfection. Along with that, the act of the servant does not occur for other than its time, because [he is] by his [occupation?] with the act and by instruments, while God, exalted, acts by Himself. And that is as God, exalted, knows by His essence and is powerful by His essence, and everyone other than Him is other than what I mentioned; were it not for that, no act would subsist in Him. And God is He who creates (yunshi') nothingness? Therefore, the estimation according to what they said is invalid. And upon the like of what I have mentioned is the matter of power, will, and all that we have explained. And another proof: that from the servant there occurs transitive action (fi'l mutawallid); cessation occurs after it by periods, like shooting and crimes. He deserves the name of killer, injurer, and shooter after the completion of the reality of his act [before? straight from? straight from God?], even if his act is not described by nature and generation; because the emergence of [one?] of the two aspects in the witnessed does not prevent the realization of the act. So the like of it [applies] in the unseen, even if it is not from that aspect, based on what we have explained of affirming a thing that is not a body, and on the permissibility of speaking about God with 'thing' even if it is not an accident. And every thing in the witnessed that is not a body is an accident by virtue of existence, not that that is its name. So the like of the first [applies]. And there is no power except with God. And also what they said is a sign of incapability, because the servant is not able over that whose effect (maf'ul) is not realized with him, just as he is not able over it without using himself by moving and stilling. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 647

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof passage. Maturidi first states a principle: the one whose action does not extend beyond the present moment (la ya'du al-waqi') is described with incapability, while the one whose action extends beyond (ya'duhu) and effects occur at his disposal is described with power. He gives the example of someone capable of opposites: such a person is more perfect in action. Then he generalizes to space: the one whose action is confined to his own sphere is inferior to the one whose action occurs in every sphere. This is the description of God as perfect. Human actions are limited to specific times because they require tools and effort (shughl), but God acts by His own essence, as He knows and is powerful by His essence. Without that, no action would be established in Him. God creates from nothing; therefore, the claim that takwin without a simultaneous created thing is a sign of incapability is invalid. Then Maturidi provides another proof from human transitive actions (fi'l mutawallid) like shooting and crimes. The agent is called killer or injurer after the act is finished and the effect occurs later. Even though the human act is not described as 'by nature' or 'generation', the temporal separation between the act and its effect does not prevent the act from being real. So analogously, God's takwin can precede the creation of the thing without implying incapability. He then addresses the issue of describing God as 'thing' (shay'), even if not a body or accident, to affirm that the unseen is comparable to the witnessed in certain respects. Finally, he refutes the objection that takwin without a simultaneous effect indicates incapability by noting that a servant cannot produce an effect without an accompanying action, but God is not like that; His command alone is sufficient.

Key Terms
العجز
القدرة
التمام
الحيز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's attribute of takwin must be accompanied by the created thing at the same moment, otherwise it indicates weakness or incapability.
Correction: Maturidi shows that an action that extends beyond the moment proves power, not weakness. God's takwin is in pre-eternity, and creation occurs at its appointed time.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what kind of action is a description of power?
A) An action that does not go beyond the actual moment.
B) An action that extends beyond the moment and produces effects at the agent's disposal.
C) An action that is confined to the agent's own sphere.
D) An action that requires instruments and time.

Key Takeaway
God's takwin is perfect because it precedes creation, proving His power, not incapability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about an area in your life where you feel you have complete control—like your career, relationships, or spiritual growth. How does the principle in this lesson expose the illusion of that control? When was the last time you saw your own 'incapability' because your effort could not extend beyond the moment?
?
The lesson says God's action is not limited by instruments or occupation, while yours is. Where are you relying on your own instruments (skills, money, status) as if they were self-sufficient? What would it look like to depend only on God's power that precedes and exceeds every moment of your life?
?
You claim to believe in God's perfect power, but do you live as if your actions can bring about lasting change without Him? Name one specific habit or goal where you have been trusting your own timeliness and instruments rather than God's takwin. What is the first step to surrender that area to His eternal power?

The Analogy from Transitive Human Acts and Affirming 'Thing' for God
Maturidi uses transitive acts and the term 'thing' to defend God's takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the example of transitive human acts (like shooting) to prove that God's takwin can precede its effect, and how he defends applying the term 'thing' to God.

Core Idea
A shooter is called a killer after the arrow hits, proving an act can precede its effect.

Maturidi provides another strong proof: consider human acts that produce delayed effects, such as shooting a person or committing a crime. Even though the act of shooting is completed before the effect (the arrow hitting the target), the agent is still called a killer or injurer after the effect occurs. This shows that an action can be attributed to an agent even if its effect is delayed. Similarly, God's takwin is real even before creation. Additionally, Maturidi addresses the issue of calling God 'a thing' (shay'), since God is not a body or accident, but the term is permissible by analogy to the witnessed world.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof
Read the section beginning with 'ودليل آخر' and understand the example of the shooter. Note that the agent is described as killer after the fact.
2
Analyze the analogy
The temporal separation between act and effect does not negate the reality of the act. Therefore, the same applies to God: takwin is real before creation.
The objection that takwin without effect is impossible is refuted.
3
Understand the 'thing' discussion
Maturidi then argues that just as we use 'thing' for non-body entities in the witnessed world (accidents), we can use 'thing' for God, even though He is not an accident. This is an analogical extension.
This is a response to those who deny that God can be called a 'thing'.
4
Refute the final objection
The claim that takwin without effect indicates incapability is false because a servant cannot produce an effect without his own action, but God's command is sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?
