6 min
The Attribute 'Rahim' is Essential, Not Derived from Acts
Al-Maturidi refutes the claim that 'Rahim' is a derived attribute from the act of creating mercy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Maturidi insists that the attribute 'Rahim' is an essential attribute of Allah, not merely a description derived from His act of creating mercy.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are real, not just descriptions based on His actions.

In this passage, Al-Maturidi confronts an opponent who claims that 'Rahim' (the Merciful) is an attribute that arises only because Allah creates mercy. The opponent argues by analogy with human actions. Al-Maturidi responds sharply, showing that this view would collapse the distinction between entities and their intrinsic attributes. Let's read his argument carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's objection
The opponent claims that 'Rahim' should be understood as a description based on the act of creating mercy, similar to how a person is described as an 'insulter' when he insults. Locate this analogy in the passage.
The opponent uses the example of insulting (شتم) or treating badly (سوده).
2
Identify Al-Maturidi's counter-argument
Al-Maturidi refutes by saying that if attributes were merely descriptions by a describer, then the reality of attributes inhering in entities (like motion, rest, union, separation) would be invalid. Find his key statement.
Notice the phrase 'ولو كانت الصفة في الحقيقة وصف الواصف'.
3
Understand the consequence
Al-Maturidi argues that attributes like motion and rest exist in entities regardless of anyone describing them. Therefore, attributes are real properties of the entity, not speech acts. Reflect on how this defends the essential nature of divine attributes.
This argument preserves the distinction between created entities and their permanent attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال : فإن قيل : لِمَ لا جعلتم الرحمة صفة في الحقيقة دون أن يقول 'رحيم'، فزعم أن 'رحيم' صفة دون الرحمة؛ إذ كل من فعل صفة الشيء فقد وصفه، كمن يشتم آخر أو يسوده أنه شتمه وسوده، فكذلك خلق الرحمة، ولا يجوز يوصف بها إذ خلقها حتى يقول إلى رحيم؛ فبذلك علمنا أن الصفة قوله إنه رحيم. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : ما أعرف هذا التائه بالصفات حتى يشرع في تفسير صفات الله، جل الله عن مثل هذا المتحير الخيال وتعالى. ولو كانت الصفة في الحقيقة وصف الواصف ليبطل قول الخلق بأن الخلق أعيان وصفات، ويبطل قوله فى الاجتماع والتفرق والحركة والسكون التى لا تخلو الأعيان عنها في إثبات حديها، إذ في خلو عن وصف واصف بها، قثبت أنها صفات تلزم الأعيان لا ما ذكر، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم قال : لم نقل إن الله إذا خلق الحمرة فى الثوب أنه جعل له صفة، كانت الحمرة صفة له جاز أن يقال إذ خلقها الله وصف الثوب بها، ومثله في الحركة والسكون، وكذا من يكتب إلى آخر يصنف طوله يجوز أن يُقال : وصفت لنا في كتابه، زعم أن هذا واضح.
Then he said: For it is said: Why did you not make mercy a real attribute without saying 'Rahim'? For he claimed that 'Rahim' is an attribute apart from mercy, because whoever does the attribute of a thing has described it, like one who insults another or treats him badly, that he insulted him and treated him badly. Similarly, creating mercy, and it is not permissible to be described by it when He created it until He says 'Rahim'. Thus we know that the attribute is His saying that He is merciful. Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: I do not know this bewildered one concerning attributes until he begins to interpret the attributes of Allah. Allah is exalted above such bewildered imagination and high. And if the attribute in reality were the description of the describer, then the saying of the creation would be invalidated—that the creation are entities and attributes—and his saying about union and separation, motion and rest, from which entities are never free in the establishment of their limits, would be invalidated. For in the absence of any describer describing them, it is established that they are attributes that adhere to the entities, not what he mentioned. And there is no power except through Allah. Then he said: Do we not say that if Allah created redness in a garment, He did not make it an attribute for Himself? The redness is an attribute for it; it is permissible to say that when Allah created it, He described the garment with it. Similarly for motion and rest. Also, one who writes to another and describes his length—it is permissible to say: He described it to us in his book. He claimed that this is clear.
Source pages p. 655

Commentary
This passage contains two objections and al-Maturidi's refutations. The first objection is from an opponent who argues that the attribute 'Rahim' should be considered a real attribute distinct from the act of creating mercy, because generally when a person performs an action that is an attribute of something, he is described by that action. For example, if someone insults another, he is described as an insulter. So if God creates mercy, one should say He is merciful because of that act. The opponent claims that the attribute is not mercy itself but God's statement that He is merciful. Al-Maturidi responds sharply, calling the questioner bewildered. He argues that if the attribute were merely the description of the describer, then the entire distinction between created entities and their attributes would collapse. For instance, union, separation, motion, and rest are attributes that adhere to entities regardless of whether anyone describes them. Thus, attributes are real properties of the entity, not just speech acts. The second objection deals with redness in a garment. The opponent suggests that if God creates redness in a garment, that redness becomes an attribute of the garment, and God is not described by it. Similarly, for motion and rest. Al-Maturidi simply notes that the opponent claims this is clear, without further critique, implying the point is obvious: attributes belong to the subject they inhere in, not to the one who causes them.

Key Terms
الرحمة (al-rahma)
رحيم (rahim)
الصفة (al-sifa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's attribute 'Rahim' is merely a description derived from His act of creating mercy, similar to how a person is described as an 'insulter' when he insults.
Correction: Al-Maturidi refutes this by showing that attributes like motion and rest exist in entities regardless of any describer, so divine attributes are real and essential, not derived from actions.

Checkpoint
What is al-Maturidi's main argument against the claim that 'Rahim' is an attribute derived from creating mercy?
A) He agrees but says it is a different kind of attribute
B) He argues that it would invalidate the distinction between entities and their intrinsic attributes
C) He says it is a matter of linguistic convention
D) He claims that mercy is not an attribute at all

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi establishes that divine attributes are real and essential, not merely descriptions based on God's acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you invoke Allah as Ar-Rahim, do you truly believe that His mercy is a real, eternal attribute of His essence, or do you secretly think of His mercy as merely a response to your actions? How would your relationship with Him change if you fully internalized that His mercy is not dependent on what you do or do not do? What commitment can you make today to live with that certainty?
?
Imagine if Allah's attributes were merely descriptions based on His acts—then His mercy would only appear after He creates mercy, leaving you uncertain of His constant character. Would you be comfortable worshiping a God whose attributes are not eternal and unchanging? What does your answer reveal about your need for a God who is inherently and unchangeably merciful?
?
Al-Maturidi warns that reducing attributes to mere descriptions would collapse the entire framework of creation and its inherent qualities. How does this refutation challenge any subtle tendencies you might have to reduce Allah to your own limited concepts? Are you willing to let go of any mental idol of a God defined by your actions, and submit to the God described by revelation as truly and eternally merciful?

The Example of Redness in a Garment
Al-Maturidi uses the example of redness in a garment to show that attributes inhere in the subject, not the agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the example of redness in a garment supports the view that attributes belong to the subject they inhere in, not to the one who causes them.

Core Idea
Created attributes inhere in creatures, not in the Creator.

Al-Maturidi presents a second objection about redness in a garment. The opponent suggests that if God creates redness in a garment, that redness becomes an attribute of the garment, and God is not described by it. Al-Maturidi mentions this example as a clear point that attributes belong to the subject they inhere in. Let's examine how this reinforces his overall argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about redness
The passage states that when Allah creates redness (حمرة) in a garment, the redness is an attribute (صفة) of the garment, not of Allah. Find this statement.
Also note the parallel to motion and rest, and the example of describing someone's length in a book.
2
Identify the point of the example
Al-Maturidi is showing that attributes belong to the subject in which they inhere. The garment is described as red because redness is in it; Allah is not described as red. This supports his earlier argument that attributes are real properties of entities.
The opponent's claim that this is clear (زعم أن هذا واضح) might be sarcastic or simply noting the obvious.
3
Connect to the broader discussion
This example illustrates that just as redness is an attribute of the garment, not of the one who creates it, so too mercy (if created) would be an attribute of the created thing, not of Allah. Therefore, 'Rahim' must be an essential attribute of Allah, not dependent on His act of creating mercy.
This strengthens Al-Maturidi's refutation of the first objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

For in the absence of any describer describing them, it is established that they are attributes that adhere to the entities, not what he mentioned. And there is no power except through Allah. This passage contains two objections and al-Maturidi's refutations. The first objection is from an opponent who argues that the attribute 'Rahim' should be considered a real attribute distinct from the act of creating mercy, because generally when a person performs an action that is an attribute of something, he is described by that action. Correction: The example shows that created attributes inhere in the creature, not in the Creator. God does not become described by what He creates.

?

?

?
Consider a description you wrote about someone. Did you ever feel that the description made you the one who possesses that trait? How can you consciously distinguish between the attribute in the description and your own essence, and apply this to how you understand Allah's attributes?

Divine Attributes
beginner
6 min
Mercy as Attribute: Objection and Maturidi's Refutation
Maturidi refutes that the attribute of mercy is the statement 'Rahim'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the claim that the attribute of mercy is merely the statement 'Rahim' rather than a real attribute inherent in the essence.

Core Idea
An attribute is not the act of describing but a real quality inherent in the essence.

This passage presents an objection that reduces Allah's attribute of mercy to the mere utterance of the word 'Rahim'. Maturidi responds by clarifying that attributes are real qualities inherent in essences, not dependent on being described. The lesson examines his reasoning and its implications for understanding divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first part of the passage (from 'ثم قال : فإن قيل...' to 'أن الصفة قوله إنه رحيم'). Notice the claim that 'Rahim' is a description without mercy, because creating mercy does not make one merciful until the word is said.
This objection treats attributes as linguistic acts.
2
Examine Maturidi's refutation
Read Maturidi's response. He dismisses the objector as confused and argues that if attributes were descriptions, it would invalidate the distinction between essences and attributes, and it would undermine our understanding of essential qualities like motion and rest.
Maturidi uses logical consequences to refute.
3
Understand the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that attributes 'adhere to essences' (تلزم الأعيان) as real properties, not as mere descriptions. Reflect on how this defends the reality of divine attributes.
This is a fundamental point in Maturidi kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال : فإن قيل : ليم لا جعلتم الرحمة صفة في الحقيقة دون أن يقول "رحيم" ، فزعم أن "رحيم" صفة دون الرحمة ؛ إذ كل من فعل صفة الشيء فقد وصفه ، كمن يشتم آخر أو يسوده أنه شتمه وسوده ، فكذلك خلق الرحمة ، ولا يجوز يوصف بها إذ خلقها حتى يقول إلى رحيم ; فبذلك علمنا أن الصفة قوله إنه رحيم
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : ما أعرف هذا التائه بالصفات حتى يشرع في تفسير صفات الله ، جل الله عن مثل هذا المتحير الخيال وتعالى . ولو كانت الصفة في الحقيقة وصف الواصف ليبطل قول الخلق بأن الخلق أعيان وصفات، ويبطل قوله فى الاجتماع والتفرق والحركة والسكون التى لا تخلو الأعيان عنها في إثبات حديها ، إذ في خلو عن وصف واصف بها، فثبت أنها صفات تلزم الأعيان لا ما ذكر ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
Then he said: For it is said: Why did you not make mercy a real attribute without saying 'Rahim'? So he claimed that 'Rahim' is a description without mercy; because whoever does the action of a thing's attribute has described it, like one who insults another or makes him chief, that he insulted him or made him chief. Similarly, the creation of mercy, and it is not permissible to be described by it when He created it until He says 'Rahim'. Thus we know that the attribute is His saying that He is Rahim.
Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: I do not know this wanderer concerning attributes so that he begins to interpret the attributes of Allah – Allah is exalted above such a bewildered imagination and transcendent. And if the attribute in reality were the description of the describer, it would invalidate the statement of creation that creations are essences and attributes, and it would invalidate his statement concerning combination, separation, motion, and rest, from which essences are never free, in establishing their limits, since there is a lack of description by a describer. Thus it is established that they are attributes that adhere to essences, not what he mentioned. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 655

Commentary
This passage begins with an objection: someone asks why the opponent did not make mercy a real attribute without saying the word 'Rahim'. The objector claims that 'Rahim' is a description without the actual attribute of mercy, arguing that whoever performs an action that is an attribute of something has described that thing—like someone who insults another or makes him chief, it is said he insulted him or made him chief. Similarly, creating mercy does not mean one is described by mercy until one says 'Rahim'. Thus the attribute, according to them, is the statement 'He is Rahim'. Maturidi responds by criticizing this understanding. He says he does not recognize this confused person as having knowledge of attributes to interpret Allah's attributes. He then argues: if the attribute in reality were the act of describing by the describer, it would invalidate the concept that created things are essences (a'yan) and attributes (sifat). It would also invalidate the opponent's statement about combination, separation, motion, and rest—from which essences are never free—in establishing their limits. Because if attributes were merely descriptions, then essences would be without inherent qualities when not described. Maturidi concludes that attributes adhere to essences themselves, not as the objector claimed. He ends with a pious phrase: 'there is no power except with Allah.'

Key Terms
صفة
رحمة
رحيم
وصف
عيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The attribute of mercy is merely the statement 'Rahim', not a real inherent quality.
Correction: Maturidi shows that attributes are real properties of essences, independent of being described. The creation of mercy itself makes the creator merciful, not the utterance of the word.

Checkpoint
According to the objector, what is the actual attribute of mercy?
A) The creation of mercy
B) The statement 'Rahim'
C) The essence of mercy
D) The act of describing

Key Takeaway
Attributes are real qualities inherent in essences, not dependent on being described by a speaker.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Ar-Rahman' in prayer, do you truly believe that mercy is an inherent quality of Allah, or do you treat it as just a word? How might your reliance on His mercy change if you internalize that His mercy is not a mere label but a real attribute that never leaves Him?
?
Maturidi criticizes those who speak about Allah's attributes without proper knowledge. Reflect on a time you might have spoken about Allah without knowledge. What will you do to ensure you seek understanding before describing Him?
?
If attributes are real and adhere to the essence, what does that imply about your own understanding of Allah's names? Commit to learning one name deeply this week and let it transform how you relate to Him.

Maturidi's Warning Against False Claims of Benefit
Maturidi opens with a warning against those who consider misguidance beneficial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's admonition that claiming benefit in misguidance invites Allah's wrath.

Core Idea
Claiming benefit in misguidance is a sign of Allah's wrath.

Maturidi begins by admonishing the believers to recognize the great wrath of Allah upon those who consider their own misguidance as beneficial. This warning sets the stage for the subsequent discussion on figurative language in divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening warning
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi addresses the believers and warns against those who claim benefit from misguidance.
The text contains some uncertain words due to OCR.
2
Identify the core admonition
Identify the phrase where Maturidi says that Allah's abandonment is considered a benefit by the misguided. Understand the irony.
This is a rhetorical device emphasizing the severity of their error.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why Maturidi starts with this warning before discussing attributes. It establishes the gravity of theological errors.
The warning is both a spiritual admonition and a contextual framing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تتم هذا النوع من حماقته التحمدوا الله معاشر إخواني على ما أكرمكم الله بمعرفته ، ولتعلموا عظيم مقت الله على من زعم من المصالح له فى الدين ، حتى لو أراد الله أن يزيد له شيئا لا يملكه مما به صلاحه لا يقدر عليه، بل به يفسد ، التتبينوا أنه جعل خذلانه صلاحا في الدين ، وإخلاله نعمة من نعم الرب جل ثناؤه
ولو قال : لم نقل إذا خلق الله الحمرة فى الثوب أنه جعل له صفة ، كانت الحمرة صفة له جاز أن يقال إذ خلقها الله وصف الثوب بها ، ومثله في الحركة والسكون ، وكذا من يكتب إلى آخر يصنف طوله يجوز أن يُقال : وصفته لنا في كتابه ، زعم أن هذا واضح .
ثم قال : وإنا لا ننكر جواز إطلاق القول بأن الحمرة صفة الأحمر ، والرحمة صفة الفعل ، لكن على المجاز ، والحقيقة ما ذكرت
ثم عورض بأنه يجوز إذا أن يكون للصفة صفة
قال : نعم ، بمعنى أنها توصف ، لكن ذلك إنما يوجد ما دام الواصف قائلا ، فإذا أمسك لا
قال الفقيه رحمه الله : تأملوا عظيم منزلة المعتزلة بهذا الذي هذا مبلغ علمه بالصفة والموصوف والمجاز والحقيقة مما لو قرن به أجهل أهل توحيد الله لاستعظمه ، ثم يقدم قومه يوم القيامة فيوردهم المورد الذى هذا وصف سبيله نسأل الله العصمة
Then this type of his foolishness is completed: praise Allah [؟], O brethren, for what He has honored you with knowledge, and learn the great wrath of Allah upon those who claim benefit for themselves in religion, such that if Allah wanted to increase something for them that they do not possess by which their benefit would be, they would not be able to do it, but rather they corrupt it. So realize that He made His abandonment a benefit in religion, and His impairment a blessing from the blessings of the Lord.
And if he said: 'We do not say when Allah creates redness in a garment that He has made it an attribute for it; redness was an attribute for it; it is permissible to say when He created it, Allah described the garment with it, and similarly for motion and rest. Likewise, one who writes to another and classifies his length, it is permissible to say: He described it to us in his book.' He claimed that this is clear.
Then he said: 'And we do not deny the permissibility of saying that redness is an attribute of the red, and mercy is an attribute of the act, but metaphorically; the reality is what I mentioned.'
Then it was objected that it is permissible then for an attribute to have an attribute.
He said: 'Yes, in the sense that it is described, but that only exists as long as the describer is speaking; if he stops, then no.'
The jurist (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'Reflect on the great rank of the Mu'tazila with this one whose knowledge of attribute and described, metaphor and reality is such that if the most ignorant of the people of tawhid were compared to him, he would consider him great, yet he leads his people on the Day of Judgment to the source that is described in this way; we ask Allah for protection.'
Source pages p. 655

Commentary
This passage begins with Maturidi addressing the believers, warning them against the opponent's foolishness. He instructs them to praise Allah for the knowledge they have been given and to recognize the great wrath of Allah upon those who claim that their own misguidance is beneficial. He then presents a new objection from the opponent: If someone says that when Allah creates redness in a garment, He has not made that redness an attribute for the garment, it is still permissible to say that Allah described the garment with the redness. Similarly for motion and rest, and for a person who writes a book describing something. The opponent claims this is clear. Maturidi responds: 'We do not deny the permissibility of saying that redness is an attribute of the red thing, and mercy is an attribute of the act, but it is metaphorical (majaz); the reality (haqiqa) is what I mentioned (i.e., the attribute is inherent in the thing itself).' Then another objection is raised: 'It is permissible then for an attribute to have an attribute.' Maturidi answers: 'Yes, in the sense that it is described, but that only exists as long as the describer is speaking; if he stops, then no (it does not have an attribute).' After this, the jurist (al-faqih) comments, urging reflection on the high rank of the Mu'tazila, who despite their ignorance, are considered great by some, yet they lead their people to a terrible fate on the Day of Judgment. He asks Allah for protection.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
خذلان
صلاح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say about those who claim benefit from misguidance?
A) They will be rewarded
B) They incur Allah's great wrath
C) They are excused due to ignorance
D) They should be praised for their effort

Key Takeaway
Maturidi warns that considering misguidance as beneficial is a grave error that invites Allah's wrath.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever convinced yourself that a small sin or compromise is actually beneficial for you in some way—maybe to fit in or achieve a goal? How does Maturidi's warning expose the self-deception in that reasoning, and will you repent from it today?
?
Are there habits or beliefs you hold that you consider beneficial to your faith, but which might actually be forms of being abandoned by Allah? What would it take for you to examine them honestly and seek His guidance?
?
Maturidi says that even if Allah wanted to increase something beneficial, the misguided would be unable to attain it. Does this description fit any area of your life where you feel spiritually stuck? Will you ask Allah to remove the veil of self-deception and grant you true benefit from Him alone?

The Permissibility of Metaphorical Attribution (Majaz)
Maturidi explains the permissibility of metaphorical attribution using examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's distinction between metaphorical (majaz) and real (haqiqa) attribution of attributes to objects.

Core Idea
Attributes like redness are metaphorically predicated, not literally.

After the initial warning, Maturidi presents an opponent's objection regarding the attribution of redness to a garment and clarifies that such attribution is permissible only as a metaphor (majaz), not as a literal reality (haqiqa). This distinction is critical for understanding how divine attributes are spoken of.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's argument
Read the passage where the opponent says that when Allah creates redness in a garment, He has not made redness an attribute of the garment, but we can still say He described the garment with it.
The opponent uses examples of redness, motion, rest, and writing a description.
2
Identify Maturidi's response
Identify Maturidi's statement that he does not deny the permissibility of saying 'redness is an attribute of the red', but only on a metaphorical basis.
He distinguishes between majaz and haqiqa.
3
Understand the distinction
Contrast the metaphorical attribution (majaz) with the real attribution (haqiqa) that Maturidi mentioned earlier. The 'reality' is that the attribute is inherent in the thing itself.
This distinction helps avoid anthropomorphism when speaking about Allah.

?

?

How might this habit affect the way you understand Allah's descriptions of Himself? What step will you take today to distinguish between metaphor and reality in your understanding of the Qur'an?

Does an Attribute Have an Attribute? Maturidi's Answer
Maturidi responds to the objection that attributes could have attributes and adds a closing warning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's response to the objection that attributes would have attributes if metaphorical attribution is allowed.

Core Idea
An attribute can be described only as long as the describer speaks.

After clarifying the metaphorical nature of certain attributions, an objection is raised: if we allow metaphorical attribution, then an attribute (like redness) could itself have an attribute (like being red). Maturidi responds by distinguishing between describing and having a real attribute. He then concludes with a reflection on the ignorance of the Mu'tazila.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection that if metaphorical attribution is permissible, then it would be permissible for an attribute to have an attribute.
The objection is a logical extension of Maturidi's position.
2
Examine Maturidi's response
Maturidi answers 'yes' but only in the sense that the attribute is being described while the describer is speaking. Once the speech stops, the description ceases.
This limits the attribution to the context of discourse.
3
Reflect on the closing comment
Read the jurist's comment about the Mu'tazila's ignorance and their fate on the Day of Judgment. Understand the warning.
This underscores the seriousness of getting these distinctions wrong.

Scriptural Proof for Allah's Speech
Maturidi cites Quranic verses and consensus for Allah's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic verses and scholarly consensus to establish that Allah speaks with real speech.

Core Idea
The Quran itself affirms that Allah spoke to Moses, and there is no denial among the creation.

Maturidi begins with the foundation: Allah's attribute of speech is established by both revelation and reason. Here he focuses on the scriptural evidence, citing direct Quranic verses and the agreement of the community. He also addresses those who question why Allah does not speak to them directly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on scriptural proof
Read the part of the source from 'فالسمع قوله' to 'يَسْمَعُونَ كَلَامَ اللهِ'. Follow the author's progression through verses and consensus.
2
Identify the primary verse
The first verse (4:164) uses the verbal noun 'تكليما' to emphasize the reality of Allah's speech to Moses. Notice how this refutes any denial.
The verbal noun form makes the action definite and emphatic.
3
Note the consensus
Maturidi states that there is agreement among the creation that Allah is a speaker and has real speech, though they differ on its nature. This consensus is a source of authority.
The nature (mahiyya) of Allah's speech is not the focus here; the reality is affirmed.
4
Understand the criticism of doubters
Maturidi criticizes those who ask 'Why does not Allah speak to us?' (2:118), calling their question arrogant and ignorant of their own rank. This shows that the demand is improper.
5
Reflect on the second verse
The verse (2:75) indicates that a group used to listen to Allah's speech, confirming that it is something that can be heard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : الأصل أن الله عز وجل قد ثبت وصفه بالكلام بحجة السمع والعقل ، فالسمع قوله وَكَلَّمَ اللهُ مُوسَى تَكْلِيمًا ذكره بالمصدر مع غير تمانع بين الخلق بكلام الله ، وقد وجد الاتفاق على أنه متكلم وأن له كلاما في الحقيقة وإن اختلفت الآراء في مائيته : ولا أنكر على الذين قالوا : لَوْلا يُكَلِّمُنَا الله إلا بوصف التكبر والجهل بمنزلة أنفسهم ، وكذلك قوله : وَقَدْ كَانَ فريقٌ مِنْهُم يَسْمَعُونَ كَلَامَ اللهِ
وأما العقل : إن كل عالم قادر لا يتكلم فعن آفة ، يكون من عجز أو والله عنه متعال ، ثبت أنه متكلم . على أن الذي لا يتكلم في الشاهد إنما لا يتكلم بالمعنى الذي لا يسمع ولا يبصر من الآفة ، والله منزه عن المعنى الذي يقتضى الصمم والعمى ، وكذلك البكم ، وهو أولى ; إذ هو أجل ما يحمد به
Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The foundation is that Allah, mighty and majestic, has established His description with speech by the proof of revelation and reason. As for revelation, His saying: 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' (4:164) mentioned in the verbal noun without any dissent among the creation regarding Allah's speech. And the agreement has been found that He is a speaker and that He has real speech, even if opinions differ on its quiddity. And I do not deny those who said: 'Why does not Allah speak to us?' (2:118) except by description of arrogance and ignorance of their own rank. Similarly, His saying: 'And a group among them used to listen to the words of Allah' (2:75).
As for reason: Every knower and powerful being who does not speak does so due to an impediment, whether from incapacity or [؟] – and Allah is exalted above that – so it is established that He is a speaker. Moreover, the one who does not speak in the witnessed world only does not speak in the sense that he does not hear or see due to an affliction. Allah is free from the meaning that necessitates deafness and blindness, and likewise dumbness. And it is more fitting, for it is the most praiseworthy thing by which He is praised.
Source pages p. 656

Commentary
This passage provides the proof for the attribute of speech (kalam). Maturidi states the foundational principle: Allah's description with speech is established by two types of evidence: sam' (revelation) and aql (reason). The scriptural proof includes the verse 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' (4:164), which uses the emphatic verbal noun (takliman) to affirm real speech without any denial among the creation. There is agreement that Allah is Mutakallim (Speaker) and has real speech, though people differ on its nature (mahiyya). Maturidi criticizes those who demand 'Why does not Allah speak to us?' (2:118) as arrogant and ignorant of their own status. He also cites the verse 'a group among them used to listen to the words of Allah' (2:75) to show that Allah's speech is heard. The rational proof: every being who knows and has power yet does not speak, does so because of an impediment, either from incapacity or from [؟] – Allah is exalted above such defects – therefore it is established that He is a speaker. In the witnessed world (shahid), one who does not speak fails due to an affliction such as deafness or blindness. Allah is free from any meaning that necessitates deafness or blindness, and likewise dumbness. Speech is more fitting for Allah, as it is the most praiseworthy attribute by which He is praised.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's speech is metaphorical or not real.
Correction: Maturidi affirms that Allah has real speech (kalam haqiqi) as shown by the emphatic verbal noun and consensus.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does Maturidi primarily use to prove that Allah speaks?
A) 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' (4:164)
B) 'Why does not Allah speak to us?' (2:118)
C) 'And a group among them used to listen to the words of Allah' (2:75)
D) 'And Allah has knowledge of all things' (2:282)

Key Takeaway
The Quran and communal consensus affirm that Allah has real speech, as He spoke to Moses directly and His words are heard.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the question of the disbelievers, 'Why does not Allah speak to us?', Maturidi called it arrogance. In your own heart, do you ever feel that Allah hasn't given you enough guidance or signs, as if you deserve a direct conversation? What would it take for you to fully accept that the Quran is your personal address from Allah, and that asking for more is a lack of gratitude? Will you today commit to treating every verse as if Allah is speaking directly to you?
?
The verse says that a group listened to the words of Allah. When you recite or hear the Quran, do you listen with the conviction that you are hearing the actual speech of your Lord, or does it become just a routine? What would change in your focus and reverence if you truly believed that every letter is from Him?
?
Maturidi emphasizes that opinions differ on the nature of Allah's speech, but the reality of speech is agreed upon. In your life, do you sometimes get caught up in debating theological details while neglecting the simple, life-altering fact that Allah speaks to you? How will you respond today to the reality that your Creator has spoken and that speech is in your hands?
